Output only the translation. <NL> English: a <NL> German:	German: ein/a/eines (depending on the context) But in most cases where "a" is used as an indefinite article in English, it can be left out entirely in German without changing the meaning of the sentence. For example, "I have a book" would translate to "Ich habe Buch", but in proper German grammar, you would say "Ich habe ein Buch". If "a" is used as a placeholder or dummy article (as in "a" in the indefinite article), it can also be translated as "ein/a/eines", depending on the gender of the noun that follows. Please provide more context for a precise translation. Without context, "a" cannot be accurately translated into German as it does not have an equivalent standalone meaning.
